[4:0:344,499] California's residents, including vulnerable and at-

[3:2:66,97] 3810 - REGIONAL OFFICES AND REGIONAL ADVISORY COMMITTEES  

[4:0:66,117] Twelve Regional Offices and Regional Advisory Committees provide administrative support and assist with advocacy, training,  

[4:1:66,127] coordination, and implementation of State Plan objectives in Council Regions throughout California. These offices and advisory  

[4:2:66,137] committees provide information and data to the Council to assess regional needs and implementation of the State Plan and for  

[4:3:66,148] inclusion in reports to the federal government and the Legislature.  

[5:0:66,168] In addition to implementation of State Plan activities, Regional Office staff support the following activities to improve and  

[5:1:66,178] enhance the availability and quality of services for residents of state developmental centers and state-operated community  

[5:2:66,188] facilities:  

[6:0:65,206] • Advocacy services through volunteers recruited by Council staff for individuals who have no legally appointed representative  

[6:1:76,216] to assist them in making choices and decisions.

[6:3:76,243] developmental disabilities are observed.

[5:0:66,154] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:0:66,172] 3820 - EMERGENCY MEDICAL SERVICES AUTHORITY  

[6:1:66,190] Disaster Medical Services Division  

[7:0:66,207] The Disaster Medical Services Division coordinates California's medical response to major disasters by carrying out the  

[7:1:66,218] Authority's mandate to provide medical resources to local governments in support of their disaster response efforts. The  

[7:2:66,228] Division coordinates with the Governor's Office of Emergency Services, the Office of Homeland Security, the California National  

[7:3:66,238] Guard, the California Department of Public Health, and other local, state, and federal agencies, private sector hospitals,  

[7:4:66,248] ambulance companies, and medical supply vendors, to promote and improve disaster preparedness and emergency medical  

[7:5:66,258] response in California.  

[8:0:66,276] Emergency Medical Services Personnel Division  

[9:0:66,294] The Emergency Medical Services Personnel Division is responsible for licensing and enforcement actions of all active  

[9:1:66,304] paramedics throughout the state. The Division develops and implements regulations that set training, certification and licensure  

[9:2:66,314] standards, and the scope of practice for various emergency medical services personnel. The Division also sets standards for,  

[9:3:66,324] and approves, training programs in: pediatric first aid, CPR,   preventive health practices for child day care providers, and school  

[9:4:66,335] bus drivers. It also develops standards for emergency medical dispatcher training, pre-arrival emergency care instructions, and  

[9:5:66,345] the epinephrine auto-injector training program.  

[9:6:66,363] Emergency Medical Services Systems Division  

[10:0:66,380] The Emergency Medical Services Systems Division is responsible for developing and implementing emergency medical  

[10:1:66,390] services systems throughout California, including the support of local Health Information Exchange projects that will allow the  

[10:2:66,401] state to collect more meaningful data so that emergency medical services providers can deliver better patient care. The  

[10:3:66,411] Division also oversees system development and implementation by the local Emergency Medical Services agencies, the  

[10:4:66,421] statewide trauma system, and emergency medical dispatcher and communication standards.   Additionally, it   establishes  

[10:5:66,431] regulations and guidelines for local agencies; reviews and approves local plans to ensure they meet the minimum state  

[10:6:66,441] standards; coordinates injury and illness prevention activities with the California Department of Public Health and the Office of  

[10:7:66,452] Traffic Safety; manages the state's emergency medical services data and quality improvement process; conducts Ambulance  

[10:8:66,462] Exclusive Operating Area evaluations; oversees the operation of California's Poison Control System; and manages the  

[10:9:66,472] Emergency Medical Services for Children programs.

[3:0:66,69] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[3:1:65,87] • Mental Health Workforce Investment—The Budget includes $47.4 million one-time General Fund   to fund scholarships and  

[3:2:76,97] loan repayment awards for mental health workforce programs. Of this amount, $1,000,000 is available specifically for former  

[3:3:76,107] foster youth.  

[4:0:65,124] • Workforce Education and Training Implementation—The Budget includes $60 million one-time ($35 million General Fund  

[4:1:76,134] and $25 million Mental Health Services Fund) to implement the 2020-2025 Five Year Workforce Education and Training  

[4:2:76,144] (WET) Plan which addresses workforce shortages in the state’s public mental health system. To be eligible for funding  

[4:3:76,154] through the plan, regional partnerships will be required to provide a 33 percent match of local funds.  

[4:4:65,170] • Primary Care Clinician Psychiatry   Fellowship—The Budget includes $2.7 million one-time General Fund   for   scholarships for  

[4:5:76,181] physicians participating in a   Primary Care Clinician Psychiatry Fellowship administered by the University of California.  

[4:6:65,197] • Pediatric Residency Programs—The Budget includes $2 million one-time General Fund   to fund grant awards at pediatric  

[4:7:76,207] residency programs.

[10:0:66,606] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[10:1:66,624] 3835 - HEALTH CARE WORKFORCE  

[11:0:66,645] The Health Care Workforce Program, through the Health Care Workforce Development Division and the Health Professions  

[11:1:66,655] Education Foundation, improves access to medical, mental, and dental health care providers in underserved areas throughout  

[11:2:66,665] California. The Program conducts research to identify areas of unmet need and administers grants that provide financial  

[11:3:66,675] incentives to individuals and institutions to increase the number of providers in those areas. The Program promotes health care  

[11:4:66,685] workforce diversity and cultural competency. It includes the following programs:  

[11:5:65,703] • Song-Brown Health Care Workforce Training Program

[4:1:66,184] 3840 - FACILITIES DEVELOPMENT  

[5:0:66,201] The Facilities Development Program safeguards public health, safety, and general welfare through regulation of the design and  

[5:1:66,211] construction of health care facilities, including compliance with seismic safety requirements, to ensure they are capable of  

[5:2:66,222] providing sustained services to the public.  

[5:3:66,239] 3845 - CAL-MORTGAGE LOAN INSURANCE  

[6:0:66,257] The Cal-Mortgage Program is modeled after federal home mortgage insurance programs and insures loans to public and  

[6:1:66,267] nonprofit health care facilities for construction, renovation, and expansion projects. The Program underwrites loans, monitors  

[6:2:66,277] the Cal-Mortgage insured loan portfolio, and administers the Health Facility Construction Loan Insurance Fund. By facilitating  

[6:3:66,288] access to private capital at no cost to taxpayers, the Program has improved the delivery of health care throughout California.  

[6:4:66,305] 3855 - HEALTH CARE INFORMATION AND QUALITY ANALYSIS 

[7:0:66,323] The Health Care Information Program sets standards for, collects, and maintains financial and utilization data from  

[7:1:66,333] approximately 6,000 licensed health facilities in California, as well as comprehensive demographic, diagnostic, and treatment  

[7:2:66,343] data for all patients discharged from licensed hospitals, treated in emergency departments, or having had an ambulatory  

[7:3:66,354] surgery procedure in hospital surgical clinics. This information is used by health care policymakers, health care providers,  

[7:4:66,364] health planners, public and private sector health care purchasers, researchers, consumers, and the media. To further this  

[7:5:66,374] mission, the Health Care Information Program is implementing new health care cost transparency data programs to collect and  

[7:6:66,384] analyze prescription drug cost data and health care payment data to improve transparency, inform policy decisions, reduce  

[7:7:66,394] disparities, and reduce health care costs. 

[7:8:66,412] 3860 - ADMINISTRATION  

[8:0:66,433] Administration provides overall management, planning, policy development, legal, legislative, information technology support  

[8:1:66,443] and administrative services to OSHPD.

[1:0:184,43] 4150   Department of Managed Health Care  

[2:0:66,64] The Department of Managed Health Care protects   health care consumers   and ensures a stable health care delivery system in  

[2:1:66,74] California. The Department achieves this mission by:  

[2:2:65,92] • Licensing and regulating the full scope of managed care models, including all Health Maintenance Organizations (HMO) in  

[2:3:76,102] the state, Preferred Provider Organizations (PPO), Exclusive Provider Organizations (EPO), Point-of-Service (POS) products  

[2:4:76,112] and Medi-Cal managed care plans. The Department also licenses and conducts financial reviews of Medicare Advantage  

[2:5:76,123] and Part D plans and licenses and regulates specialized health plans including chiropractic, dental, vision, psychological  

[2:6:76,133] (behavioral health) and pharmacy.  

[2:7:65,149] • Enforcing the Knox-Keene Health Care Service Plan Act of 1975, as amended.  

[2:8:65,165] • Conducting medical surveys and financial examinations to verify that health plans are complying with the law and are  

[2:9:76,175] financially stable to serve their enrollees.  

[2:10:65,192] • Operating a 24-hour-a-day Help Center to resolve health care consumer complaints and administer the Independent Medical  

[2:11:76,202] Review program.  

[2:12:65,218] • Reviewing proposed health plan rate changes for sufficient justification and reasonableness.  

[2:13:65,234] • Monitoring the financial solvency of the medical groups with whom health plans contract to provide health benefits to their  

[2:14:76,244] enrollees.  

[3:0:65,261] • Convening the Financial Solvency Standards Board, comprised of people with expertise in the medical, financial and health  

[3:1:76,271] plan industries, to advise the Director on strategies to keep the managed care industry financially stable.

[6:0:66,243] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,261] 3870 - HEALTH PLAN PROGRAM  

[7:0:66,282] The Health Plan Program's primary objective is to regulate managed health care plans and assist consumers to resolve  

[7:1:66,292] disputes with health plans. The program's key functions to achieve this objective are to: license managed health care plans,  

[7:2:66,302] conduct routine and non-routine financial exams and medical surveys, review proposed premium rate increases, assist  

[7:3:66,312] consumers with health care issues and enable managed health care patients to receive the medical care and services to which  

[7:4:66,323] they are entitled, and operate a consumer services toll-free complaint line (1-888-466-2219).

[0:0:66,13] 2019-20 STATE BUDGET — HHS   26   HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:228,43] 4170   Department of Aging  

[2:0:66,64] The Department of Aging's mission is to promote the independence and well-being of older adults, adults with disabilities, and  

[2:1:66,74] families through:  

[3:0:65,92] • Access to information and services to improve the quality of their lives,  

[3:1:65,108] • Opportunities for community involvement,  

[3:2:65,124] • Support to family members providing care, and  

[3:3:65,141] • Collaboration with other state and local agencies.  

[4:0:66,158] As the federally designated State Unit on Aging, the Department administers federal Older Americans Act programs that  

[4:1:66,168] provide a wide variety of community-based supportive services and administers the Health Insurance Counseling and  

[4:2:66,179] Advocacy Program. The Department also administers two Medi-Cal programs: it contracts directly with agencies that operate  

[4:3:66,189] the Multipurpose Senior Services Program (MSSP) and provides oversight for the MSSP waiver, and certifies Community-

[4:4:66,199] Based Adult Services centers for participation in Medicaid.  

[5:0:66,219] The Department administers most of these programs through contracts with the state's 33 local Area Agencies on Aging. At the  

[5:1:66,230] local level, Area Agencies on Aging contract for and coordinate this array of community-based services to older adults, adults  

[5:2:66,240] with disabilities, family caregivers, and residents of long-term care facilities.

[6:0:66,157] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[6:1:65,175] • Senior Nutrition Program—The Budget includes $17.5 million General Fund for the Senior Nutrition program, which provides  

[6:2:76,185] meals to seniors in both congregate and home-delivered settings.   The increased funding for the program   will be suspended  

[6:3:76,195] on December 31, 2021. The suspension will be lifted if the Administration determines through the 2021 Budget Act process  

[6:4:76,205] that there is sufficient General Fund revenue to support all suspended programs in the subsequent two fiscal years. 

[6:5:65,222] • Multipurpose Senior Services Program—The Budget includes $29.6 million ($14.8 million General Fund) one-time to provide  

[6:6:76,232] three years of supplemental provider payments for Multipurpose Senior Services Program providers.  

[6:7:65,248] • Long-Term Care Ombudsman Program—The Budget includes $4.2 million General Fund in 2019-20 and $5.2 million  

[6:8:76,258] General Fund annually thereafter for local Long-Term Care Ombudsman programs to provide quarterly visits to skilled  

[6:9:76,268] nursing facilities and residential care facilities for the elderly.  

[7:0:65,285] • Aging and Disability Resource Connection Grants—The Budget includes $5 million General Fund to provide grants to local  

[7:1:76,295] Area Agencies on Aging and Independent Living Centers to complete the planning and application process to become Aging  

[7:2:76,305] and Disability Resource Connections, which utilize the “No Wrong Door” model.   The increased funding for grants will be  

[7:3:76,315] suspended on December 31, 2021. The suspension will be lifted if the Administration determines through the 2021 Budget  

[7:4:76,325] Act process that there is sufficient General Fund revenue to support all suspended programs in the subsequent two fiscal  

[7:5:76,336] years. 

[8:0:65,352] • Dignity at Home Fall Prevention Program—The Budget includes $5 million General Fund one-time to provide grants to local  

[8:1:76,362] Area Agencies on Aging for injury prevention education and home modifications for seniors who are at risk of falling or  

[8:2:76,372] institutionalization.

[5:0:66,218] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,236] 3890 - NUTRITION  

[6:0:66,256] The Nutrition Program provides nutritionally-balanced meals, nutrition education, and nutrition counseling to individuals 60  

[6:1:66,266] years of age or older. In addition to promoting better health through improved nutrition, the program focuses on reducing the  

[6:2:66,277] isolation of the elderly and providing a link to other social and supportive services such as transportation, information and  

[6:3:66,287] assistance, employment, and education.  

[6:4:66,304] 3895 - SENIOR COMMUNITY EMPLOYMENT SERVICE  

[7:0:66,325] The federal Senior Community Service Employment Program, Title V of the Older Americans Act, provides part-time subsidized  

[7:1:66,335] training and employment in community service agencies for low-income persons 55 years of age and older. The program also  

[7:2:66,345] promotes transition to unsubsidized employment.  

[7:3:66,363] 3900 - SUPPORTIVE SERVICES  

[8:0:66,381] This program provides supportive services in the community to adults 60 years of age or older, their family caregivers,  

[8:1:66,391] grandparents caring for grandchildren, and residents of long-term care facilities. Services include information and assistance,  

[8:2:66,401] legal assistance, transportation, respite in-home support, senior center activities, elder abuse prevention, and the Long-Term  

[8:3:66,411] Care Ombudsman. Older Americans Act Titles III and VII fund these services to enable individuals to access the support  

[8:4:66,421] necessary for them to remain independent in their communities, continue in their caregiving role, and/or receive long-term care  

[8:5:66,432] services appropriate to their needs.  

[8:6:66,449] 3905 - COMMUNITY-BASED PROGRAMS AND PROJECTS  

[9:0:66,467] This program includes the community-based Health Insurance Counseling and Advocacy Program (HICAP). HICAP provides  

[9:1:66,477] personalized counseling, community education, and outreach events for Medicare beneficiaries. HICAP is the primary local  

[9:2:66,487] source for accurate and objective information and assistance with Medicare benefits, prescription drug plans, and health plans.  

[9:3:66,505] 3910 - MEDI-CAL PROGRAMS  

[10:0:66,523] This program includes oversight of the Multipurpose Senior Services Program (MSSP) and Community-Based Adult Services  

[10:1:66,533] (CBAS) program. CBAS is a community-based day health program that provides services to adults 18 years of age or over who  

[10:2:66,543] are at risk of needing institutional care due to chronic medical, cognitive, or mental health conditions and/or disabilities. The  

[10:3:66,553] Department certifies CBAS centers for participation in the Medi-Cal Program. Under a 1915(c) Medicaid home and community-

[10:4:66,564] based services waiver, MSSP provides health and social care management to prevent premature and unnecessary long-term  

[10:5:66,574] care institutionalization of frail adults aged 65 or older who otherwise would be placed in a nursing facility.

[11:1:66,585] 3930 - COMMISSION ON AGING  

[12:0:66,603] The Commission's statutory responsibilities include: assisting with the development of the Department of Aging's State Plan on  

[12:1:66,613] Aging, monitoring the plan's progress, and information-gathering. As part of its information-gathering responsibility, the  

[12:2:66,624] Commission holds meetings and public hearings around the state to address the issues and concerns of older Californians,  

[12:3:66,634] their families, and caregivers. The Commission uses the information gathered from these meetings and public hearings to  

[12:4:66,644] develop initiatives and projects focused on older Californians and their caregivers. The Commission also assisted with the  

[12:5:66,654] development and implementation of the state's Alzheimer's Disease Plan, holds membership on the California Family  

[12:6:66,664] Caregiver Task Force, and administers the Area Agency on Aging Council of California. The Area Agency on Aging Council of  

[12:7:66,675] California is supported solely by voluntary contributions made through a check-off box included on the state income tax form.

[1:0:169,43] 4260   State Department of Health Care Services  

[2:0:66,64] The mission of the   State Department of Health Care Services (DHCS) is to provide Californians with access to affordable,  

[3:0:66,74] integrated, high-quality health care, including medical, dental, mental health, substance use treatment services, and long-term  

[3:1:66,84] care. To fulfill its mission, DHCS finances and administers a number of individual health care service delivery programs,  

[4:0:66,95] including the state's Medicaid Program (Medi-Cal), which provides health care services to low-income persons and families  

[4:1:66,105] who meet defined eligibility requirements.

[8:0:66,487] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[9:0:66,505] 3960010 - MEDICAL CARE SERVICES (MEDI-CAL)  

[10:0:66,526] Medi-Cal is responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of health care services to low-income Californians. Medi-Cal  

[10:1:66,536] provides access to quality medical care in a fiscally prudent manner through both fee-for-service and managed care delivery  

[10:2:66,546] systems. Medi-Cal activities are carried out through the following divisions: Integrated Systems of Care; Managed Care Quality  

[10:3:66,556] and Monitoring; Managed Care Operations; Medi-Cal Eligibility; Medi-Cal Dental Services; Pharmacy Benefits; Benefits; Safety  

[10:4:66,566] Net Financing; Capitated Rates Development; Fee-For-Service Rates Development;   Behavioral Health Financing; Behavioral  

[10:5:66,577] Health Community Services;   Fiscal Forecasting;   Medi-Cal Behavioral Health; Audits and Investigations; California Medicaid  

[10:6:66,587] Management Information Systems; Provider Enrollment; Research and Analytic Studies; Third Party Liability and Recovery;  

[10:7:66,597] Information Management; and Clinical Assurance and Administrative Support. Additional Program Offices include: the Office of  

[10:8:66,607] Family Planning.  

[11:0:66,625] 3960023 - CHILDREN'S MEDICAL SERVICES  

[12:0:66,643] Children's Medical Services is responsible for coordinating and directing the delivery of health care services to low-income and  

[12:1:66,653] seriously ill children, including the Child Health and Disability Prevention Program, the Genetically Handicapped Persons  

[12:2:66,663] Program, and the California Children's Services Program. These services are provided through the Integrated Systems of Care  

[12:3:66,673] Division.

[2:0:66,64] The California Department of Public Health (Public Health) is dedicated to optimizing the health and well-being of all  

[2:1:66,74] Californians through the following core activities:  

[3:0:65,92] • Protecting the public from communicable diseases.  

[4:0:65,108] • Protecting the public from unhealthy and unsafe environments.  

[5:0:65,124] • Preventing disease, disability, and premature death; and reducing or eliminating health disparities.  

[5:1:65,141] • Preparing for and responding to public health emergencies.  

[6:0:65,157] • Producing and disseminating data to evaluate population health status; inform people, institutions and communities; and to  

[6:1:76,167] guide public health strategies, programs, and actions.  

[7:0:65,183] • Promoting healthy lifestyles for individuals and families in their communities and workplaces.  

[7:1:65,199] • Providing access to quality, population-based health services.  

[8:0:66,217] Because Public Health's programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Department has a capital outlay program to  

[8:1:66,227] support this need. For the specifics on the Department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure Overview."

[4:0:66,269] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[5:0:65,287] • Alzheimer’s Disease Program Grants and Governor's Task Force on Brain Health — The Budget includes ongoing $3 million  

[5:1:76,297] General Fund for the Alzheimer's Disease Program to support research grants, with a focus on research to understand the  

[5:2:76,307] greater prevalence of Alzheimer's among women and communities of color. The funding will also support the creation and  

[5:3:76,318] implementation of the Governor's Task Force on Brain Health. Additionally, the Budget includes one-time $5 million General  

[5:4:76,328] Fund, available over three years, for grants to develop Alzheimer’s disease local infrastructure.  

[6:0:65,344] • Black Infant Health Program Expansion — The Budget includes ongoing $19.4 million ($7.5 million General Fund) to expand  

[6:1:76,354] the Black Infant Health Program, including the California Perinatal Equity Initiative, to improve African-American infant and  

[6:2:76,364] maternal health.  

[7:0:65,381] • California Home Visiting Program Expansion — The Budget includes ongoing $45.9 million ($23 million General Fund) to  

[7:1:76,391] expand the California Home Visiting Program to increase participation and provide a wider range of home visiting models  

[7:2:76,401] based on varying family needs.  

[8:0:65,417] • Emergency Preparedness, Response, and Recovery — The Budget includes ongoing $959,000 ($569,000 General Fund) to  

[8:1:76,427] support health care facilities and mass care shelters prepare, respond, and recover during public health emergencies.  

[9:0:65,444] • Infectious Diseases Prevention and Control — The Budget includes one-time $40 million General Fund, available over four  

[9:1:76,454] years, for infectious diseases prevention and control and ongoing $2 million General Fund specifically to address sexually  

[9:2:76,464] transmitted diseases. Additionally, the Budget includes ongoing $5 million General Fund each for sexually transmitted  

[9:3:76,474] disease, human immunodeficiency virus, and hepatitis C virus prevention and control, subject to suspension on December  

[9:4:76,484] 31, 2021, unless the Administration determines through the 2021 budget process that there is sufficient General Fund  

[9:5:76,495] revenue to support all suspended programs and activities.  

[10:0:65,511] • Licensing and Certification: Los Angeles County Contract — The Budget includes an additional $17.2 million Licensing and  

[10:1:76,521] Certification Program Fund for a new, expanded contract with the Los Angeles County Department of Public Health to  

[10:2:76,531] perform licensing and certification activities in Los Angeles County.

[5:0:66,393] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,411] 4040010 - Emergency Preparedness  

[6:0:66,429] The Public Health Emergency Preparedness program coordinates preparedness and response activities for all public health  

[6:1:66,439] emergencies, including natural disasters, acts of terrorism, and pandemic diseases. The program plans and supports surge  

[6:2:66,449] capacity in the medical care and public health systems to meet needs during emergencies. The program also administers  

[6:3:66,460] federal and state funds that support Public Health emergency preparedness activities.  

[6:4:66,477] 4045 - PUBLIC AND ENVIRONMENTAL HEALTH  

[7:0:66,487] The Public and Environmental Health programs provide public health services of: communicable disease control; chronic  

[7:1:66,498] disease and injury prevention; environmental public health; maternal, child, and family health; and vital records. These  

[7:2:66,508] programs function as part of the greater public health system throughout California.  

[7:3:66,526] 4045010 - Healthy Communities  

[8:0:66,543] This program works to prevent and control chronic diseases, injuries, and violence. Chronic diseases include cancer,  

[8:1:66,553] cardiovascular diseases, asthma, oral diseases, and diabetes. The areas of focus for this program include: reducing the  

[8:2:66,564] prevalence of obesity; improving oral health; reducing and preventing tobacco use; developing the local public health  

[8:3:66,574] workforce; preventing and controlling injuries, violence, deaths, and diseases related to behavioral, environmental, and  

[8:4:66,584] occupational factors; promoting and supporting safe and healthy environments in all communities and workplaces; and  

[8:5:66,594] preventing and treating problem gambling. This program includes Chronic Disease and Injury Control Division, Environmental  

[8:6:66,604] and Occupational Disease Control Division and the Office of Problem Gambling.  

[8:7:66,622] 4045023 - Infectious Diseases  

[9:0:66,640] This program works to prevent and control infectious diseases such as: HIV/AIDS, viral hepatitis, influenza and other vaccine-

[9:1:66,650] preventable illnesses, sexually transmitted diseases, tuberculosis, emerging infections, and foodborne illnesses. This program  

[9:2:66,660] includes Communicable Disease Control, the Office of AIDS, the Office of Binational Border Health, and the Office of Refugee  

[9:3:66,670] Health.

[10:1:66,709] and postpartum women, infants, children, and adolescents and their families. This program includes Genetic Disease

[0:0:66,13] 2019-20 STATE BUDGET — HHS   128   HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:176,43] 4300   Department of Developmental Services  

[2:0:66,64] The Department of Developmental Services is responsible under the Lanterman Developmental Disabilities Services Act for  

[2:1:66,74] providing persons with developmental disabilities the services and supports they need to lead more independent and  

[2:2:66,84] productive lives and to make choices and decisions about their lives. The Department sets broad policy and provides  

[2:3:66,95] leadership for developmental services statewide; establishes priorities, standards, and procedures within which the  

[2:4:66,105] developmental services program operates; monitors, reviews, and evaluates service delivery; and helps to remediate problems  

[2:5:66,115] that arise. Services are delivered through a statewide network of 21 private, nonprofit, locally based community agencies  

[2:6:66,125] known as regional centers as well as through developmental centers and a state-operated community facility. The Department,  

[2:7:66,135] through the 21 regional centers, oversees coordination of services to persons with developmental disabilities; provides that  

[2:8:66,146] such services are planned, provided, and meet the needs and choices of these individuals at each stage of their lives; and, to  

[2:9:66,156] the extent possible, accomplishes these goals in the individual's home community.  

[3:0:66,174] The Department has a capital outlay program to support its state operated facilities and the infrastructure investment. For the  

[3:1:66,184] specifics on the Department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure Overview."

[2:0:141,32] 4300   Department of Developmental Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,88] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[4:0:65,106] • Supplemental Rate Increases and Developmental Services System Accountability and Oversight—The Budget includes  

[4:1:76,116] $206.7 million ($125 million General Fund) in 2019-20 and $413.3 million ($250 million General Fund) in 2020-21 to provide  

[4:2:76,127] supplemental rate increases to providers across a broad array of service categories. The increased funding provides a  

[4:3:76,137] broad-based increase of up to 8.2 percent for service categories identified in the developmental services rate study  

[4:4:76,147] submitted to the Legislature in March 2019. The increased funding for developmental services provider rates will be  

[4:5:76,157] suspended on December 31, 2021. The suspension will be lifted if the Administration determines through the 2021 Budget  

[4:6:76,167] Act process that there is sufficient General Fund revenue to support all suspended programs in the subsequent two fiscal  

[4:7:76,178] years.  

[5:0:65,194] • Headquarters Restructure and Reorganization—The Budget includes $8.1 million ($6.5 million General Fund) ongoing for a  

[5:1:76,204] reorganization of departmental headquarters to strengthen oversight and monitoring of regional centers and provider  

[5:2:76,214] operations and enhance program compliance.  

[6:0:65,230] • Uniform Holiday Schedule Suspension—The Budget includes $50.3 million ($30.1 million General Fund) in 2019-20 to  

[6:1:76,241] suspend implementation of the Uniform Holiday Schedule. The increased funding will be suspended on December 31, 2021.  

[6:2:76,251] The suspension will be lifted if the Administration determines through the 2021 Budget Act process that there is sufficient  

[6:3:76,261] General Fund revenue to support all suspended programs in the subsequent two fiscal years.  

[7:0:65,277] • Acute and Mobile Crisis Services—The Budget includes $5.3 million ($4.8 million General Fund) and $7.9 million ($4.7  

[7:1:76,287] million General Fund) annually thereafter to expand crisis services to the Central Valley.  

[8:0:65,304] • Development of Community Crisis Homes for Children—The Budget includes $4.5 million one-time General Fund to develop  

[8:1:76,314] community crisis housing specifically for children.  

[9:0:65,330] • Specialized Home Monitoring—The Budget includes $5.8 million ($3.9 million General Fund) ongoing to increase monitoring  

[9:1:76,340] of Enhanced Behavioral Support Homes and Community Crisis Homes.  

[10:0:65,356] • Specialized Caseload Ratios—The Budget includes $3.8 million ($2.6 million General Fund) ongoing to establish a reduced  

[10:1:76,367] regional center service coordinator caseload ratio for consumers with specialized behavioral needs.  

[11:0:65,383] • Best Buddies—The Budget includes $2 million General Fund to support social inclusion, integrated employment, and  

[11:1:76,393] leadership program services for children and adults with developmental disabilities, and will include a report of the number of  

[11:2:76,403] persons served annually with these funds.

[6:0:66,487] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,505] 4140 - COMMUNITY SERVICES PROGRAM  

[7:0:66,525] Through the network of regional centers, the Department supports the development and maintenance of services for eligible  

[7:1:66,536] persons with developmental disabilities who reside in the community. The regional centers directly provide or coordinate the  

[7:2:66,546] following services and supports: (1) information and referral, (2) assessment and diagnosis, (3) counseling, (4) lifelong  

[7:3:66,556] individualized planning and service coordination, (5) purchase of necessary services included in the individual program plan,  

[7:4:66,566] (6) assistance in finding and using community and other resources, (7) advocacy for the protection of legal, civil, and service  

[7:5:66,576] rights, (8) early intervention services for infants and their families, (9) family support, (10) planning, placement, and monitoring  

[7:6:66,587] for 24-hour out-of-home care, (11) training and educational opportunities for individuals and families, (12) community education  

[7:7:66,597] about developmental disabilities, and (13) habilitation services.  

[8:0:66,615] 4145 - STATE-OPERATED RESIDENTIAL AND COMMUNITY FACILITIES PROGRAM  

[9:0:66,632] The Department currently operates two residential facilities: Fairview Developmental Center (Orange County) and Porterville  

[9:1:66,642] Developmental Center (Tulare County). Secure treatment services are provided at the Porterville Developmental Center  

[9:2:66,653] for   individuals who have been found incompetent to stand trial due to their developmental disability. The Department also  

[9:3:66,663] operates four Stabilization, Training, Assistance, and Reintegration (STAR) residences, and will develop three additional  

[9:4:66,673] residences in Northern and   Central California   to provide acute crisis services in the community. The Department also leases  

[9:5:66,683] one small community facility for persons who require specialized behavioral interventions: Canyon Springs, a 63-bed facility in  

[9:6:66,693] Cathedral City (Riverside County).  

[10:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

# === PAGE 133 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:66,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:407,13] 2019-20 STATE BUDGET — HHS   131 

[2:0:141,32] 4300   Department of Developmental Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] All   residential facilities are licensed as General Acute Care Hospitals with distinct parts for skilled nursing care and intermediate  

[3:1:66,79] care. Canyon Springs operates as an intermediate care facility, and STAR residences operate as community crisis homes.  

[3:2:66,89] Services at all facilities involve the provision of active treatment through residential and day programs on a 24-hour basis,  

[3:3:66,99] including appropriate medical and dental care, health maintenance activities, and assistance with activities of daily living,  

[3:4:66,109] training, education, and employment.  

[4:0:66,127] Individuals served in the STAR crisis   residences are committed by a court order to the Department for suitable treatment and  

[4:1:66,137] habilitation services during a crisis, and are provided services and supports necessary to prepare them for return to their  

[4:2:66,148] residential home or to transition to a new living option. The primary objective of this program   is to provide a safety net of  

[4:3:66,158] services that include providing care, treatment, crisis services, and habilitation services to residents based upon assessed  

[4:4:66,168] need and as outlined in each person's Individual Program Plan. These services are offered in the most efficient, effective, and  

[4:5:66,178] least restrictive manner to all individuals referred by the regional centers and/or the judicial system; and are designed to teach  

[4:6:66,188] individuals the skills for increased independence, provide for preservation or improvement of health and welfare, and enhance  

[4:7:66,199] personal competence in all areas of daily living.  

[5:0:66,216] Fairview Developmental Center and the non-secure treatment portion of Porterville Developmental Center are scheduled for  

[5:1:66,226] closure no later than 2021.  

[6:0:66,244] 4149 - PROGRAM ADMINISTRATION  

[7:0:66,265] The objective of this program is to: (1) provide overall management, planning and policy development, legal, legislative, audit,  

[7:1:66,275] and administrative services; (2) manage revenue and reimbursement collections from federal and state programs, insurance  

[7:2:66,285] companies, and private payers for the cost of services; (3) monitor regional center operations for compliance with statute,  

[7:3:66,295] regulations, and their contract with the Department; (4) provide central administrative and clinical management services to  

[7:4:66,305] the   two residential facilities and the leased small community facility to oversee the quality of services provided, compliance with  

[7:5:66,316] state licensing and federal certification requirements, protection of consumers and staff, and maintenance of facility structures  

[7:6:66,326] and grounds; and (5) oversee areas that include the development of policy and procedures for developmental center  

[7:7:66,336] operations, law enforcement and protective services, facility population management, program and fiscal oversight, and facility  

[7:8:66,346] planning and support.  

[8:0:66,364] 4150 - DEPARTMENT OF JUSTICE LEGAL SERVICES PROGRAM  

[9:0:66,382] This program provides legal support for the Department through an interagency agreement with the Department of Justice.  

[9:1:66,399] 9900100 - ADMINISTRATION  

[10:0:66,417] The objective of this program is to provide: (1) overall management, planning and policy development, legal, legislative, audit,  

[10:1:66,427] and administrative services, and (2) revenue and reimbursement collections from federal and state programs, insurance  

[10:2:66,437] companies, and private payers for the cost of services.

[10:0:66,560] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[11:0:66,578] The Department of Developmental Services is responsible for the operation and maintenance of the facilities under its control,  

[11:1:66,588] including three state-owned and operated 24-hour care facilities and related buildings, grounds, and infrastructure. The facilities  

[11:2:66,599] are Fairview Developmental Center in Orange County, Porterville Developmental Center in Tulare County, and Sonoma  

[12:0:66,609] Developmental Center in Sonoma County. The developmental centers are comprised of approximately 3.6 million gross square  

[12:1:66,619] feet in 437 buildings on 1,647 acres in total. As of December 2018, Sonoma Developmental Center in Sonoma County had  

[12:2:66,629] transitioned all former residents to community living.   The Department will continue to maintain the property until June 30,  

[12:3:66,639] 2019.   In addition, the Department operates   one residence, and will develop   six more, for the Stabilization, Training,  

[13:0:66,650] Assistance, and Reintegration beds that provide acute crisis services in the community. The Department is also responsible for  

[13:1:66,660] the maintenance of interior finishes and equipment at a 57,000 square foot-leased facility in Riverside County. These facilities  

[13:2:66,670] are used to aid the Department's mission to provide medical, dental, and nursing care; active treatment; supervision; education;  

[13:3:66,680] and vocational training for residents with developmental disabilities.

[1:0:201,43] 4440   Department of State Hospitals  

[2:0:66,64] The Department of State Hospitals manages the nation's largest inpatient forensic mental health hospital system. Its mission is  

[2:1:66,74] to provide evaluation and treatment in a safe and responsible manner, seeking innovation and excellence in state hospital  

[2:2:66,84] operations, across a continuum of care. The Department is responsible for the daily care and provision of mental health  

[2:3:66,95] treatment for its patients in five state hospitals located in Atascadero, Coalinga, Metropolitan-Los Angeles, Napa, and  

[3:0:66,105] Patton,   and employs over 11,000 staff. Additionally, the Department provides services in jail-based competency treatment  

[3:1:66,115] programs and conditional release programs throughout the 58 counties. In 2017-18, the Department served approximately  

[3:2:66,125] 12,000 patients within state hospitals and jail-based facilities, with average daily censuses of 5,897 and 227 respectively. The  

[3:3:66,135] conditional release program (CONREP) reflected an average daily census of approximately 654.  

[4:0:66,153] Because the Department of State Hospitals' programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Department has a capital  

[4:1:66,163] outlay program to support this need. For the specifics on the Department's capital outlay program see "Infrastructure  

[4:2:66,174] Overview."

[1:0:407,13] 2019-20 STATE BUDGET — HHS   141 

[2:0:166,32] 4440   Department of State Hospitals - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[4:0:65,87] • Metropolitan State Hospital Bed Expansion—The Budget includes $15.5 million General Fund and 99.2 positions for the  

[4:1:76,97] second and final expansion phase of the Metropolitan State Hospital’s secured treatment area.   When completed in 2019, a  

[4:2:76,107] total of 236 additional secured forensic beds will be available for the treatment of incompetent to stand trial commitments.  

[5:0:65,124] • Mission-Based Review: Direct Care Nursing—The Budget includes $15 million General Fund and 117.3 positions for the first  

[5:1:76,134] year of a three-year phase-in to staff 128 medication rooms and to provide nighttime nursing supervisors in units across the  

[5:2:76,144] five state hospitals. This will increase the number of direct-care nursing staffing in an effort   to reduce patient violence, staff  

[5:3:76,154] injuries, and staff turnover and absenteeism. In addition, the Budget includes 304 positions to better reflect the State  

[5:4:76,164] Hospital's usage of temporary help staff. 

[6:0:65,181] • Jail-Based Competency Treatment Programs—The Budget includes $6.4 million General Fund to contract for up to 73  

[6:1:76,191] additional jail-based competency restoration treatment beds through both existing and new county jail treatment programs.  

[7:0:65,207] • Patient-Driven Operating Expenses—The Budget includes $11 million General Fund for increased patient-driven operating  

[7:1:76,217] expenses and equipment costs, such as pharmaceuticals, outside medical costs, and food. In addition, the Budget includes  

[7:2:76,227] a standard estimate methodology for determining State Hospital patient operating expenses and equipment needs, which is  

[7:3:76,238] being applied beginning in 2019-20.  

[8:0:65,254] • Mission-Based Review: Court Evaluations and Reports—The Budget includes $8.1 million General Fund and 43 positions for  

[8:1:76,264] the first year of a three-year phase-in of additional staff dedicated to forensic evaluations, court reports and testimony, court  

[8:2:76,274] report coordination, and neuropsychological assessments and treatment. These dedicated staff will result in consistent  

[8:3:76,284] evaluations and reports statewide, and reduce the amount of time treating clinicians spend in court, enabling them to focus  

[8:4:76,295] on patient treatment.  

[9:0:65,311] • Mission-Based Review: Workforce Development—The Budget includes $1.8 million total fund and 8 positions to: (1) expand  

[9:1:76,321] partnerships with community colleges to increase capacity in existing Psychiatric Technician training programs, and (2)  

[9:2:76,331] establish a Forensic Psychiatry Residency program at Napa State Hospital.  

[10:0:65,347] • Conditional Release Step Down Program—An increase of $5.7 million General Fund in 2019-20 ($11.5 million General Fund  

[10:1:76,358] annually thereafter) for the Department of State Hospitals to contract for a 78-bed community step-down program to serve  

[10:2:76,368] Mentally Disordered Offenders and Not Guilty by Reason of Insanity commitments who are preparing for conditional release  

[10:3:76,378] from state hospitals within 18 to 24 months. This funding also includes increasing an existing Department of State Hospitals’  

[10:4:76,388] contract by 4 beds.

[2:0:166,32] 4440   Department of State Hospitals - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] The state hospital system includes five state hospitals: Atascadero, Metropolitan-Los Angeles, Napa, Patton, and Coalinga. In  

[3:1:66,79] addition, until July 1, 2017, this program included three inpatient psychiatric programs located at the California Medical Facility  

[3:2:66,89] in Vacaville, Salinas Valley State Prison in Salinas Valley and within the California Health Care Facility in Stockton. The three  

[3:3:66,99] psychiatric programs provide treatment services to CDCR inmates and the responsibility for these facilities transferred to  

[3:4:66,109] CDCR beginning in 2017-18. Mental health treatment services at all facilities are delivered by clinical teams who provide full-

[3:5:66,120] time inpatient care to the most serious mentally ill and those incapable of living in the community.  

[4:0:66,137] 4380028 - CONDITIONAL RELEASE 

[5:0:66,155] The Conditional Release Program (CONREP) is the statewide system of community-based services for specified forensic  

[5:1:66,165] patients. Mandated as a state responsibility by the Governor's Mental Health Initiative of 1984, the program began operations  

[5:2:66,175] on January 1, 1986. The goal of CONREP is to provide greater public protection in California communities via a standardized  

[5:3:66,186] community outpatient treatment system.  

[6:0:66,203] 4385 - EVALUATION AND FORENSIC SERVICES  

[7:0:66,221] Evaluation and Forensic Services is comprised of the Mentally Disordered Offender (MDO) program and the Sex Offender  

[7:1:66,231] Commitment Program (SOCP). The MDO program applies only to prisoners whose crimes were committed on or after January  

[7:2:66,241] 1, 1986. Penal Code Sections 2960-2981 require that a prisoner who meets six specific criteria be ordered by the Board  

[7:3:66,252] of   Parole Hearings   to be treated by State Hospitals as a condition of parole. Welfare and Institutions Code Section 6600 et seq.  

[7:4:66,262] (Chapter 793, Statutes of 1995) was enacted January 1, 1996, establishing a new category of civil commitment for persons  

[7:5:66,272] found, upon release from prison, to be sexually violent predators (SVP). The SOCP administers clinical screenings to  

[7:6:66,282] determine whether an individual is likely to be a SVP and warrants forensic psychological evaluations by the Department.  

[8:0:66,300] 4390 - LEGAL SERVICES  

[9:0:66,318] The Legal Services Division is responsible for providing a full range of comprehensive legal services including, but not limited  

[9:1:66,328] to: litigation; developing legislation; protecting the confidentiality and privacy of patient information under the Health Information  

[9:2:66,338] Portability and Accountability Act; providing contract law advice to the state hospitals   and headquarters; and representing the  

[9:3:66,348] Department at various court and administrative law proceedings involving involuntary medication, orders to show cause, and  

[9:4:66,358] personnel actions statewide.  

[10:0:66,376] 4400 - ADMINISTRATION  

[11:0:66,394] Department of State Hospitals Headquarters oversees the California state hospital system, which provides mental health  

[11:1:66,404] services to patients admitted into Department of State Hospitals facilities. Program Administration includes headquarters  

[11:2:66,414] functions such as: policy development and management, licensing oversight, patients' rights coordination, clinical oversight,  

[11:3:66,424] data research, fiscal, personnel and contracts management, as well as legal services.  

[12:0:66,442] Hospital Administration includes centralized functions and services that directly affect patient care but are administered  

[12:1:66,452] centrally from headquarters.  

[13:0:66,470] 4400010 - HEADQUARTERS ADMINISTRATION  

[14:0:66,488] Department of State Hospitals Headquarters oversees the California state hospital system, which provides mental health  

[14:1:66,498] services to patients admitted into   its facilities. Headquarters Administration includes headquarters functions such as: policy  

[14:2:66,508] development and management, licensing oversight, patients' rights coordination, clinical oversight, data research, fiscal,  

[14:3:66,518] personnel and contracts management, as well as legal services.  

[15:0:66,536] 4400020 - HOSPITAL ADMINISTRATION  

[16:0:66,554] Department of State Hospitals Headquarters includes a Hospital Administration component. Hospital Administration includes  

[16:1:66,564] centralized functions and services that directly affect patient care but are administered centrally from headquarters such as:  

[16:2:66,574] technology services, hospital police and fire oversight, patient referral management, clinical recruitment, patient benefit and  

[16:3:66,584] billing management, and Medicare revenue collection.  

[17:0:66,602] 4410 - STATE HOSPITALS  

[18:0:66,620] The state hospital system includes five state hospitals located at Atascadero, Metropolitan-Los Angeles, Napa, Patton, and  

[18:1:66,630] Coalinga. Mental health treatment services at all facilities are delivered by clinical teams who provide full-time inpatient care to  

[18:2:66,640] those with mental illness and those incapable of living in the community. The state hospitals treat the following types of  

[18:3:66,650] patients: civil commitments under the Lanterman-Petris-Short Act (LPS); forensic commitments such as incompetent to stand  

[18:4:66,661] trial (IST), not guilty by reason of insanity (NGI), sexually violent predators (SVP), and mentally disordered offenders (MDO);  

[18:5:66,671] and prisoners with mental illness ( Coleman ) from CDCR.

[2:0:166,32] 4440   Department of State Hospitals - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] The Department of State Hospitals-Atascadero opened in 1954 and is located on the Central Coast of California in Atascadero  

[3:1:66,79] (San Luis Obispo County). The hospital is a self-contained psychiatric hospital constructed within a security perimeter. The  

[3:2:66,89] majority of the all-male patient population is remanded for treatment by   Superior Courts or by CDCR pursuant to various  

[3:3:66,99] sections of the California Penal Code   and the Welfare and Institutions Code.  

[4:0:66,117] DSH-Atascadero primarily serves the following four patient types: MDO,  Coleman   patients from CDCR, IST, and   NGI.  

[5:0:66,135] 4410020 - COALINGA  

[6:0:66,152] The Department of State Hospitals-Coalinga opened in 2005 and is located on the western edge of Fresno County. The  

[6:1:66,163] hospital is California’s newest forensic mental health hospital and was created to primarily treat SVPs. It is a self-contained  

[6:2:66,173] psychiatric hospital constructed with a security perimeter. CDCR provides perimeter security as well as transportation of  

[6:3:66,183] patients to outside medical services and court proceedings. The majority of the all-male patient population is remanded for  

[6:4:66,193] treatment by   Superior Courts or CDCR pursuant to various sections of the California Penal Code and the Welfare and  

[6:5:66,203] Institutions Code.  

[7:0:66,221] DSH-Coalinga primarily serves MDOs,  Coleman   patients from CDCR,   and SVPs.  

[8:0:66,239] 4410030 - METROPOLITAN  

[9:0:66,256] The Department of State Hospitals-Metropolitan opened in 1916 and is located in Norwalk (Los Angeles County). The hospital  

[9:1:66,267] is an open style campus within a security perimeter. Due to concerns raised by the community, DSH-Metropolitan maintains a  

[9:2:66,277] formal agreement with the City of Norwalk and the Los Angeles County Sheriff not to accept patients charged with murder or a  

[9:3:66,287] sex crime, or that are at high risk for escape.  

[10:0:66,305] DSH-Metropolitan primarily serves the following four patient types: LPS, IST, MDO, and NGI.  

[11:0:66,322] 4410040 - NAPA  

[12:0:66,340] The Department of State Hospitals-Napa opened in 1875 and is located in Napa County. The hospital   was the first of the  

[12:1:66,350] five   State Hospitals, and is   the oldest California state hospital still in operation.   It has an open style campus with a security  

[12:2:66,361] perimeter.  

[13:0:66,378] DSH-Napa primarily serves the following four patient types: LPS, IST, MDO, and NGI.  

[14:0:66,396] 4410050 - PATTON  

[15:0:66,414] The Department of State Hospitals-Patton opened in 1893 and is located in San Bernardino County. The hospital has an open  

[15:1:66,424] style campus with a security perimeter. CDCR correctional officers provide perimeter security and transportation at DSH-Patton  

[15:2:66,434] as well as transportation of patients to outside medical services and some court proceedings.  

[16:0:66,452] DSH-Patton primarily serves the following four patient types: LPS, IST, MDO, and NGI.  

[17:0:66,469] 4410060 - HOSPITAL POLICE OFFICER ACADEMY  

[18:0:66,487] The Department of State Hospitals Police Officer (HPO) Academy is overseen by the Office of Protective Services, which is a  

[18:1:66,497] full service law enforcement agency that protects the safety and security of the state hospital facilities, staff and patients. DSH  

[18:2:66,508] provides training standards, model programs, cultural competency, program development, and a comprehensive training plan  

[18:3:66,518] to all protective services staff. The HPO Academy requires that cadets successfully complete 548 hours of multidisciplinary  

[18:4:66,528] training specific to the DSH police officer job specifications.  

[19:0:66,546] 4420 - CONDITIONAL RELEASE PROGRAM  

[20:0:66,566] The Conditional Release Program is the statewide system of community-based services for specified forensic patients.  

[20:1:66,576] Mandated as a state responsibility by the Governor's Mental Health Initiative of 1984, the program began operations on  

[20:2:66,586] January 1, 1986.  

[21:0:66,604] 4420010 - CONDITIONAL RELEASE PROGRAM  

[22:0:66,622] The Conditional Release Program General/Non-Sexually Violent Predators is comprised of Not Guilty by Reason of Insanity,  

[22:1:66,632] Mentally Disordered Offender, felony Incompetent to Stand Trial, and Mentally Disordered Sex Offender patients. Individuals  

[22:2:66,642] suitable for this program may be recommended by the state hospital medical director to the courts for outpatient treatment.  

[22:3:66,652] Currently, DSH contracts with seven county-operated and three private organizations   serving all 58 counties in the state with  

[22:4:66,663] non-SVP commitments.

[3:0:66,69] 2003,   conditional release providers did not have treatment services that would allow them to accept sexually violent predators

[3:5:66,127] 4430 - CONTRACTED PATIENT SERVICES  

[4:0:66,148] The Department of State Hospitals contracts with local entities to provide mental health services to some of its patients outside  

[4:1:66,158] of state hospital facilities. This includes both the   Admissions, Evaluation, and Stabilization Center in the Kern County as well as  

[4:2:66,168] various other   jail-based competency treatment programs.  

[4:3:66,186] 4430010 - ADMISSION, EVALUATION, STABILIZATION CENTER 

[5:0:66,203] The Admissions, Evaluation, and Stabilization Center in the Kern County Jail receives incompetent to stand trial patients  

[5:1:66,214] committed to the Department of State Hospitals directly from catchment counties in southern California. Patients receive a full  

[5:2:66,224] evaluation upon admission to determine whether they can be treated through the Admissions, Evaluation, and Stabilization  

[5:3:66,234] Center on a short-term basis or may need longer-term state hospital treatment. Patients considered to be short-term can be  

[5:4:66,244] treated and discharged directly from the Admissions, Evaluation, and Stabilization Center.  

[5:5:66,262] 4430020 - JAIL-BASED COMPETENCY TREATMENT  

[6:0:66,280] The Jail-Based Competency Treatment Program focuses on defendants deemed incompetent to stand trial and provides  

[6:1:66,290] mental health treatment to defendants in county jails, restoring them to competency, and allowing for participation in court  

[6:2:66,300] proceedings.  

[7:0:66,318] 4440 - EVALUATION AND FORENSIC SERVICES  

[8:0:66,335] Evaluation and Forensic Services is comprised of the Mentally Disordered Offender and the Sex Offender Commitment  

[8:1:66,346] Programs. Penal Code Sections 2960-2981 require that a prisoner who meets specific criteria be ordered by the Board of  

[8:2:66,356] Parole Hearings to be treated by State Hospitals as a condition of parole. The Department of State Hospitals performs  

[8:3:66,366] evaluations to determine if individuals may meet the statutory criteria for the Mentally Disordered Offender program. These  

[8:4:66,376] evaluations are used by the Board of Parole Hearings in determining whether a prisoner is committed to the Department of  

[8:5:66,386] State Hospitals as a condition of parole. Welfare and Institutions Code Section 6600 et seq. (Chapter 793, Statutes of 1995)  

[8:6:66,397] was enacted January 1, 1996, establishing a new category of civil commitment for persons found, upon release from prison, to  

[8:7:66,407] be sexually violent predators. The Sex Offender Commitment Program administers clinical screenings and performs  

[8:8:66,417] evaluations to determine if prisoners may meet the statutory criteria for a sexually violent predator commitment to the  

[8:9:66,427] Department of State Hospitals upon completion of their prison term. Superior Courts make the ultimate determination whether  

[8:10:66,437] an individual is likely to be a sexually violent predator and warrants forensic psychological evaluations by the Department of  

[8:11:66,448] State Hospitals.

[5:0:66,130] INFRASTRUCTURE OVERVIEW  

[6:0:66,148] The Department of State Hospitals oversees five state hospitals.   The Department's   five state hospitals are Atascadero,  

[6:1:66,159] Coalinga, Metropolitan - Los Angeles, Napa, and Patton. These five state hospitals comprise more than 6.6 million gross  

[6:2:66,169] square feet of space on 2,600 acres of land and 474 buildings. Additionally,   the Department   provides services in jail-based  

[6:3:66,179] competency treatment programs and conditional release programs serving all 58 counties.

[5:0:66,167] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,185] 4181 - ENERGY PROGRAMS  

[6:0:66,206] The Energy Programs assist low-income households in meeting their immediate and long-term home energy needs through  

[6:1:66,216] financial assistance, energy conservation, weatherization and renewable energy services.  

[7:0:66,236] The Low-Income Home Energy Assistance Program (LIHEAP) provides financial assistance to eligible low-income households  

[7:1:66,247] to offset the costs of heating and/or cooling residential dwellings, assistance for weather-related or energy-related  

[7:2:66,257] emergencies, and weatherization services to improve the energy efficiency of low-income residential dwellings and safeguard  

[7:3:66,267] the health and safety of household occupants. This program may include a leveraging incentive program in which  

[7:4:66,277] supplementary LIHEAP funds can be obtained by LIHEAP grantees if non-federal leveraged home energy resources are used  

[7:5:66,287] along with LIHEAP weatherization related services.  

[8:0:66,308] The Department of Energy Weatherization Assistance Program provides weatherization to improve the energy efficiency of low-

[8:1:66,318] income residential dwellings and safeguard the health and safety of household occupants.  

[8:2:66,336] The Low-Income Weatherization Program (LIWP) provides weatherization and renewable energy services in low-income  

[8:3:66,346] single-family and multi-family dwellings within disadvantaged communities to help reduce greenhouse gas emissions. LIWP  

[8:4:66,356] includes projects such as weatherization and solar water heater and solar photovoltaic systems installations.  

[8:5:66,374] 4185 - COMMUNITY SERVICES  

[9:0:66,394] The Community Services Block Grant is designed to enable local government and private nonprofit community organizations to  

[9:1:66,404] help low-income families achieve and maintain self-sufficiency through a broad range of activities. These activities include  

[9:2:66,415] education, employment services, emergency services, housing, income support and management, and health and nutritional  

[9:3:66,425] services. Additionally, Community Services Block Grant funds are used by local community organizations to revitalize low-

[9:4:66,435] income communities.  

[10:0:66,453] The California Earned Income Tax Credit (Cal EITC) benefits low-income, working Californians by providing cash-back tax  

[10:1:66,463] credits to boost the income of eligible families. In 2017-18 and 2018-19, CSD has worked with the Franchise Tax Board and  

[10:2:66,473] non-profit and community-based organizations to increase awareness of the Cal EITC and provide free tax preparation  

[10:3:66,483] assistance to Californians.  

[11:0:66,524] DETAILED EXPENDITURES BY PROGRAM

[1:0:187,43] 4800   California Health Benefit Exchange  

[2:0:66,64] The California Health Benefit Exchange/Covered California mission is to increase the number of insured Californians, improve  

[2:1:66,74] health care quality, lower costs, and reduce health disparities through an innovative, competitive marketplace that empowers  

[2:2:66,84] consumers to choose the health plan and providers that give them the best value.  

[3:0:66,105] Covered California is a public entity within state government with a five-member board appointed by the Governor and  

[3:1:66,115] Legislature. Per Government Code section 100503(o), the board authorizes a budget to pay program expenses from the  

[3:2:66,125] California Health Trust Fund to administer the Exchange.

[6:0:66,191] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,210] 4201 - CALIFORNIA HEALTH BENEFIT EXCHANGE  

[7:0:66,230] The California Health Benefit Exchange is responsible in part for the implementation of the federal Patient Protection and  

[7:1:66,240] Affordable Care Act. Specifically, it facilitates the enrollment of qualified individuals and small employers in qualified health  

[7:2:66,250] plans in the individual and small employer markets. Eligible consumers can obtain qualified health plan coverage with advance  

[7:3:66,261] payment of the premium tax credit established by the federal Internal Revenue Code.  

[7:4:66,278] 4202 - STATE SUBSIDY PROGRAM  

[8:0:66,296] The State Subsidy Program provides state subsidies through the state-based health insurance exchange, also known as  

[8:1:66,306] Covered California, to qualified individuals with household incomes below 600 percent of the federal poverty level.

[0:0:66,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[1:0:407,13] 2019-20 STATE BUDGET — HHS   169 

[2:0:170,32] 5160   Department of Rehabilitation - Continued 

[3:0:66,76] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:0:66,94] 4210 - VOCATIONAL REHABILITATION SERVICES  

[5:0:66,115] The Vocational Rehabilitation Services Program delivers vocational rehabilitation services to persons with disabilities through  

[5:1:66,125] vocational rehabilitation professionals in district and branch offices located throughout the state. In addition, the Department  

[5:2:66,135] has cooperative agreements with state and local agencies (education, mental health, and welfare) to provide services to  

[5:3:66,145] consumers. The Department operates under a federal Order of Selection process, which gives priority to persons with the most  

[5:4:66,156] significant disabilities.  

[6:0:66,176] Persons with disabilities who are eligible for the Department's vocational rehabilitation services may be provided a full range of  

[6:1:66,186] services, including vocational assessment, assistive technology, vocational and educational training, job placement, and  

[6:2:66,196] independent living skills training to maximize their ability to live and work independently within their communities.  

[7:0:66,217] The Department provides comprehensive training and technical assistance to enable persons who are blind or visually  

[7:1:66,227] impaired to support themselves in the operation of vending stands, snack bars, and cafeterias. Prevocational services are  

[7:2:66,237] provided by the Orientation Center for the Blind to newly blind adults to prepare them for vocational rehabilitation services and  

[7:3:66,247] independent living.  

[8:0:66,268] The Department works with public and private organizations to develop and improve community-based vocational rehabilitation  

[8:1:66,278] services for the Department's consumers. The Department sets standards, certifies Community Rehabilitation Programs, and  

[8:2:66,288] establishes fees for services provided to its consumers.  

[9:0:66,309] The Department works with the federal government to administer two grant programs. The Promoting the Readiness of Minors  

[9:1:66,319] in Supplemental Security Income grant develops projects to promote positive outcomes for children who receive Supplemental  

[9:2:66,329] Security Income and their families. The CA Innovations Program seeks to increase the self-sufficiency of students with  

[9:3:66,339] disabilities by providing work-based learning experiences and planned education to prepare them for workplace success.  

[10:0:66,357] 4215 - INDEPENDENT LIVING SERVICES  

[11:0:66,377] The Department funds, administers, and supports 28 non-profit independent living centers in communities located throughout  

[11:1:66,388] California. Each independent living center provides services necessary to assist consumers to live independently   with full  

[11:2:66,398] inclusion   in their communities. Core services consist of information and referral, peer counseling, individual and systems  

[11:3:66,408] change advocacy, independent living skills, housing assistance, personal assistance referral services, transition and diversion  

[11:4:66,418] services to community based living, and   transition services to postsecondary life for youth.  

[12:0:66,439] The Department administers and supports the Traumatic Brain Injury (TBI) Program. In coordination with consumers and their  

[12:1:66,449] families, seven service providers throughout California provide a coordinated post-acute care service model for persons with  

[12:2:66,459] TBI, including supported living, community reintegration, vocational supportive services, public awareness, and support for  

[12:3:66,469] family, friends, and professionals within the TBI community.  

[13:0:66,490] The Department administers the federal Older Individuals Who Are Blind program that supports 19 non-profit community-based  

[13:1:66,500] organizations throughout California that provide blindness-related independent living services necessary to assist visually  

[13:2:66,510] impaired consumers age 55 or older to live independently and be productive in their communities. Core services consist of low  

[13:3:66,520] vision training, assistive technology devices and training, orientation and mobility, communication skills, independent living  

[13:4:66,530] skills development, self-advocacy, adjustment counseling, transportation, and supportive services.  

[14:0:66,548] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION  

[15:0:66,566] The Administration Program provides overall management planning, policy development, and administrative support services  

[15:1:66,576] to departmental programs.

[2:0:144,32] 5175   Department of Child Support Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,76] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[3:1:66,94] 4260 - CHILD SUPPORT SERVICES PROGRAM  

[4:0:66,112] The Child Support Services program establishes the system and process for encouraging and, when necessary, enforcing  

[4:1:66,122] parental responsibilities by establishing paternity for children, establishing court orders for financial and medical support, and  

[4:2:66,133] enforcing those orders. The program operates as the single state entity designed to administer the federally mandated Title IV-

[4:3:66,143] D child support program in California. Operation of this program is required for the state to continue to receive the Temporary  

[4:4:66,153] Assistance for Needy Families block grant.  

[4:5:66,171] 4260010 - CHILD SUPPORT ADMINISTRATION:  

[5:0:66,188] The Child Support Administration program provides funding for the salaries and benefits for local and state staff, and operating  

[5:1:66,199] expenses and equipment for the operation of California's child support program, including local child support agencies. The  

[5:2:66,209] federal government provides 66 percent of the funding and the state funds 34 percent of the administration costs.  

[5:3:66,226] 4260019 - CHILD SUPPORT AUTOMATION:  

[6:0:66,244] Pursuant to Federal law, the Department created a single, statewide child support automation system that meets federal  

[6:1:66,254] certification. There are two components of the statewide system: the Child Support Enforcement system and the State  

[6:2:66,265] Disbursement Unit. The enforcement system provides local child support staff tools to manage child support customer accounts  

[6:3:66,275] and locate and intercept assets of non-custodial parents delinquent in their child support payments. The Child Support  

[6:4:66,285] Automation program provides funding for the vendor-operated state disbursement unit, which collects child support payments  

[6:5:66,295] from non-custodial parents and disburses payments to custodial parties. In addition, the Child Support Automation program  

[6:6:66,305] provides funding for electronic data processing maintenance and operation costs at local agencies.

[0:0:66,13] 2019-20 STATE BUDGET — HHS   184 

[1:0:419,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:166,32] 5180   Department of Social Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,79] 4285-Disability Evaluation and Other Services:  

[3:1:66,89] Federal Laws: Social Security Act (Titles II, XVI, XIX).  

[4:0:66,126] MAJOR PROGRAM CHANGES  

[5:0:65,144] • CalWORKs Maximum Aid Payment (MAP) Increase—The Budget includes $331.5 million General Fund and federal  

[5:1:76,154] Temporary Assistance for Needy Families (TANF) block grant funds in 2019-20 and $441.8 million ongoing to increase  

[5:2:76,165] CalWORKs MAP levels, effective October 1, 2019.  

[6:0:65,181] • Update the CalWORKs Earned Income Disregard and Income Reporting Threshold—The Budget includes $6.8 million  

[6:1:76,191] General Fund in 2019-20 growing to $99 million General Fund ongoing beginning in 2022-23, to increase the current  

[6:2:76,201] CalWORKs Earned Income Disregard using a phased approach, from the current $225 per month in 2019-20 to $600 per  

[6:3:76,211] month in 2021-22. The Budget also aligns the CalWORKs Income Reporting Threshold with the CalFresh program at 130  

[6:4:76,222] percent of the federal poverty level beginning in 2019-20.  

[7:0:65,238] • Increase CalWORKs Asset Test Limits—Increases the CalWORKs eligibility limit on cash assets from $2,250 to $10,000 and  

[7:1:76,248] the vehicle asset limit from $9,500 to $25,000 for purposes of program eligibility, effective June 1, 2020. The revised asset  

[7:2:76,258] limit levels will be adjusted annually for inflation. The Budget includes $7.5 million General Fund in 2019-20 to reflect the  

[7:3:76,268] increased limits. Costs are estimated to be $29.9 million General Fund ongoing beginning in 2021-22.  

[8:0:65,285] • Elimination of Consecutive Day Use Requirement in the CalWORKs Homeless Assistance Program (HAP)—The Budget  

[8:1:76,295] includes $14.7 million General Fund in 2019-20 and $27.6 million ongoing General Fund to eliminate the requirement that  

[8:2:76,305] the 16 allowable days of CalWORKs temporary homeless assistance be used consecutively in a year-long period.  

[9:0:65,321] • CalWORKs Home Visiting Program—The Budget includes $89.6 million General Fund and federal TANF block grant funds in  

[9:1:76,331] 2019-20 and approximately $167 million ongoing for the CalWORKs Home Visiting Program.  

[10:0:65,348] • CalWORKs Single Allocation Budgeting Methodology—The Budget includes $41.4 million General Fund and federal TANF  

[10:1:76,358] block grant funds in 2019-20 to reflect the adoption of a revised budgeting methodology for the employment services  

[10:2:76,368] component of the CalWORKs Single Allocation to counties. Additionally, beginning in 2020-21, the Single Allocation will no  

[10:3:76,378] longer include the Stage One Child Care component. Stage One will be budgeted separately within the CalWORKs program.  

[11:0:65,394] • CalWORKs Outcomes and Accountability Review (Cal-OAR)—The Budget includes $13.2 million General Fund and federal  

[11:1:76,405] TANF block grant funds in 2019-20 for counties to perform required continuous quality improvement activities consistent with  

[11:2:76,415] Cal-OAR implementation.  

[12:0:65,431] • CalWORKs Stage One Child Care—The Budget includes $56.4 million General Fund in 2019-20 and $70.5 million ongoing  

[12:1:76,441] General Fund to improve access to and utilization of CalWORKs Stage One child care services.  

[13:0:65,457] • Supplemental Security Income (SSI) Cash-Out Policy Reversal Adjustments—The Budget preserves ongoing funding for  

[13:1:76,468] county administration and benefits for newly eligible CalFresh recipients, Supplemental Nutrition Benefit program recipients,  

[13:2:76,478] Transitional Nutrition Benefit program recipients, and California Assistance Program for Immigrants program recipients as a  

[13:3:76,488] result of expanding CalFresh eligibility to SSI recipients, effective June 1, 2019. The Budget includes $120 million General  

[13:4:76,498] Fund in 2019-20 and approximately $115 million annually thereafter to fund these programs on an ongoing basis.  

[14:0:65,514] • SSI Advocacy—The Budget includes $25 million General Fund ongoing for the Housing and Disability Advocacy Program, to  

[14:1:76,525] assist homeless, disabled individuals in applying for disability benefit programs.  

[15:0:65,541] • IHSS Restoration—The Budget includes $357.6 million General Fund in 2019-20 to restore the 7-percent across-the-board  

[15:1:76,551] reduction to IHSS service hours. The increased funding for IHSS service hours will be suspended on December 31, 2021.  

[15:2:76,561] The suspension will be lifted if the Administration determines through the 2021 Budget Act process that there is sufficient  

[15:3:76,571] General Fund revenue to support all suspended programs in the subsequent two fiscal years.  

[16:0:65,588] • County IHSS Maintenance-of-Effort Adjustment—The Budget includes an increase of $296.8 million General Fund in  

[16:1:76,598] 2019-20 to rebench the County IHSS Maintenance-of-Effort, growing to $615.3 million General Fund in 2022-23. 

[17:0:65,614] • Electronic Visit Verification—The Budget includes $37.5 million ($6.4 million General Fund) in 2019-20 to comply with the  

[17:1:76,624] federal electronic visit verification mandate and make necessary changes to the Case Management, Information and  

[17:2:76,634] Payrolling System. 

[18:0:65,651] • IHSS County Administration—The Budget includes an ongoing increase of $15.4 million General Fund for IHSS county  

[18:1:76,661] administration to reflect revised benefit rate assumptions.  

[19:0:65,677] • Federal Title IV-E Funds for Dependency Counsel—The Budget includes $34 million ongoing federal funds to support court-

[19:1:76,687] appointed dependency counsel representing children and parents during dependency proceedings.  

[20:0:65,703] • Foster Care Emergency Assistance—The Budget includes $25.8 million one-time General Fund and federal TANF block  

[21:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:76,69] grant funds in 2019-20 to provide caregivers with up to four months of emergency assistance payments pending resource
