[5:0:65,152] • Family Urgent Response System—The Budget includes $15 million General Fund in 2019-20 and $30 million General Fund  

[5:1:76,162] annually thereafter to implement a statewide hotline and enhanced county-based mobile response systems targeting youth  

[5:2:76,172] in foster care and their caregivers. The system is intended to prevent placement disruptions, reduce traumatic experiences  

[5:3:76,183] for foster youth, and reduce law enforcement calls and needless criminalization of youth. The increased funding for Family  

[5:4:76,193] Urgent Response will be suspended on December 31, 2021. The suspension will be lifted if the Administration determines  

[5:5:76,203] through the 2021 Budget Act process that there is sufficient General Fund revenue to support all suspended programs in the  

[5:6:76,213] subsequent two fiscal years.  

[6:0:65,229] • Foster Parent Recruitment, Retention, and Support—The Budget includes $21.6 million one-time General Fund in 2019-20  

[6:1:76,240] for activities and services to retain, recruit, and support foster parents, relative caregivers, and resource families. 

[7:0:65,256] • Emergency Child Care Bridge—The Budget includes an increase of $10 million General Fund for the Emergency Child Care  

[7:1:76,266] Bridge program.  

[8:0:65,282] • Bringing Families Home—The Budget includes $25 million one-time General Fund, available over three years, for the  

[8:1:76,292] Bringing Families Home Program, which is a county-optional program that provides housing-related supports to eligible  

[8:2:76,303] families served by county child welfare agencies. 

[9:0:65,319] • Immigration Services—The Budget includes a total of $65 million ongoing General Fund to support qualified nonprofit  

[9:1:76,329] organizations that provide a broad array of legal services and remedies related to immigration status for individuals and  

[9:2:76,339] families. Of   this amount, the Budget allows for up to $5 million General Fund, on a one-time basis, to be available for the  

[9:3:76,349] provision of legal services to unaccompanied undocumented minors and Temporary Protected Status beneficiaries, and $7  

[9:4:76,360] million ongoing General Fund will be used to support persons on California State University campuses. Additionally, the  

[9:5:76,370] Budget includes $25 million one-time General Fund for the Rapid Response Program to support entities that provide critical  

[9:6:76,380] assistance/services to immigrants during emergent situations when federal funding is not available.

[2:0:166,32] 5180   Department of Social Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,76] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:0:66,94] 4270 - WELFARE PROGRAMS  

[5:0:66,115] The Department's public assistance programs provide financial assistance to California residents who are unable to support  

[5:1:66,125] themselves. These programs are comprised of five components:  

[6:0:65,143] • California Work Opportunity and Responsibility to Kids (CalWORKs)  

[7:0:65,159] • Other Assistance Payments, including Foster Care, Adoption Assistance Program, Refugee Cash Assistance, and Food  

[7:1:76,169] Assistance Programs  

[8:0:65,185] • Supplemental Security Income/State Supplementary Payment Program  

[9:0:65,202] • County Administration and Automation Projects  

[10:0:65,218] • Disaster Relief  

[11:0:66,246] The objectives of these programs are to provide temporary financial assistance to eligible needy and dependent persons to  

[11:1:66,256] enable achievement of self-sufficiency or to provide safe living environments for vulnerable adults and children, and to monitor,  

[11:2:66,266] administer, and improve the quality of all welfare services.  

[12:0:66,284] 4270010 - CalWORKs:  

[13:0:66,301] The CalWORKs program is California's version of the federal Temporary Assistance for Needy Families program. CalWORKs is  

[13:1:66,312] California's largest cash aid program for children and families and is designed to provide temporary assistance to meet basic  

[13:2:66,322] needs, such as shelter, food, and clothing, in times of crisis, while encouraging personal responsibility. CalWORKs includes  

[13:3:66,332] specific welfare-to-work requirements and provides supportive services, such as child care, to enable an individual to meet  

[13:4:66,342] these requirements. Child care services currently are provided through a three-stage system to current and former CalWORKs  

[13:5:66,352] recipients with children through the age of 10 (or up to 12 under certain conditions). Stage One is administered by the  

[13:6:66,363] Department of Social Services. Stages Two and Three are administered by the California Department of Education. Parents  

[13:7:66,373] have the right to choose child care among center-based, family child care homes, or license-exempt providers. CalWORKs  

[13:8:66,383] families are then able to meet both goals of moving from welfare into the work force and engaging children in child care and  

[13:9:66,393] development services.  

[14:0:66,411] 4270019 - Other Assistance Payments:  

[15:0:66,429] The Foster Care program provides assistance payments to relatives, foster family homes, foster family agencies, short-term  

[15:1:66,439] residential treatment centers or group homes for children who have been removed from the custody of a parent or guardian as  

[15:2:66,449] a result of a judicial order or voluntary placement agreement due to findings of abuse, neglect or exploitation. This program is  

[15:3:66,459] administered by the counties in accordance with regulations, standards, and procedures set by the Department of Social  

[15:4:66,469] Services as authorized by federal and state law. The Kinship Guardianship Assistance Program provides support payments to  

[15:5:66,480] relative guardians of children who were previously in the foster care system.  

[16:0:66,497] The Adoption Assistance Program provides financial assistance to families adopting a child with special needs or to facilitate  

[16:1:66,508] the adoption of children who otherwise would remain in long-term foster care. This program is administered by the counties in  

[16:2:66,518] accordance with regulations, standards, and procedures set by the Department of Social Services as authorized by federal and  

[16:3:66,528] state law.  

[17:0:66,546] California also provides cash assistance to eligible refugee/entrant populations via the following programs:  

[18:0:65,563] • The Refugee Cash Assistance provides cash grants to refugees/entrants in their first eight months in the United States  

[18:1:76,574] provided they are not otherwise eligible for categorical welfare programs.  

[19:0:65,591] • The Unaccompanied Refugee Minors program provides culturally and linguistically appropriate child welfare, foster care, and  

[19:1:76,601] independent living services to minors who do not have parents in the United States, or who enter the United States  

[19:2:76,612] unaccompanied by a parent, an immediate adult relative, or an adult having documentable legal evidence of custody of the  

[19:3:76,622] minor.  

[20:0:65,640] • The Trafficking and Crime Victims Assistance Program provides cash aid and social services to noncitizen victims of human  

[20:1:76,650] trafficking, domestic violence and other serious crimes who meet the income and eligibility requirements. Benefits are  

[20:2:76,660] available for a maximum period of eight months for adults without children and up to 48 months for families (under  

[20:3:76,670] CalWORKs).  

[21:0:66,688] The CalFresh Program, federally referred to as the Supplemental Nutrition Assistance Program, provides improved levels of  

[21:1:66,698] nutrition among eligible low-income households by offering them a benefit amount, posted to a debit card, for the purpose of  

[21:2:66,708] purchasing food. The cost of CalFresh benefits is provided by the United States Department of Agriculture for populations  

[22:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

# === PAGE 194 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:66,13] 2019-20 STATE BUDGET — HHS   192 

[1:0:419,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES 

[2:0:166,32] 5180   Department of Social Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] eligible to receive federal benefits. Legal immigrants who meet program eligibility criteria but are ineligible for federal benefits  

[3:1:66,79] due to their immigration status are served under the state-funded program known as the California Food Assistance Program.  

[3:2:66,89] The CalFresh Employment and Training Program requires certain non-assistance CalFresh recipients to participate in  

[3:3:66,99] employment and training activities.  

[4:0:66,117] The Emergency Food Assistance Program provides commodities to local food banks in all 58 California counties for distribution  

[4:1:66,127] to the working poor, low-income, unemployed, and homeless persons. The food is distributed to eligible recipients for  

[4:2:66,137] household consumption or used to prepare and serve meals in congregate settings. This program is also supplemented with  

[4:3:66,148] food purchased by food banks using private donations, funds provided by the state, taxpayer contributions generated through a  

[4:4:66,158] state income tax check-off, as well as surplus fresh fruits and vegetables donated by farmers and businesses.  

[5:0:66,175] The Commodity Supplemental Food Program is a federally funded program for local non-profit agencies to provide nutritious  

[5:1:66,186] supplemental foods to low-income, elderly people at least 60 years of age. Administrative responsibility for the Commodity  

[5:2:66,196] Supplemental Food Program was transferred from the California Department of Education to the Department of Social Services  

[5:3:66,206] on October 1, 2016.  

[6:0:66,224] 4270028 - Supplemental Security Income/State Supplementary Payment Program:  

[7:0:66,241] The federal Supplemental Security Income (SSI) program is a cash assistance program for low-income aged, blind, or disabled  

[7:1:66,252] persons who meet the program's income and resource requirements. California supplements the federal SSI payment with a  

[7:2:66,262] State Supplementary Payment (SSP). The SSI/SSP program is administered by the federal Social Security Administration who  

[7:3:66,272] determines eligibility, computes grants, and disburses the combined monthly payment to recipients.  

[8:0:66,290] 4270037 - County Administration and Automation Projects:  

[9:0:66,307] Federal, state, and county governments share the cost of operating expenses and the salaries and benefits of county staff who  

[9:1:66,318] administer public assistance programs.  

[10:0:66,335] Federal, state, and county funds are used to finance major data automation projects of the Department of Social Services.  

[11:0:66,353] 4270046 - Disaster Relief:  

[12:0:66,371] The objective of the Disaster Relief Program is to provide monetary assistance to individuals and households who have  

[12:1:66,381] suffered eligible losses from a Presidentially-declared disaster that are not covered by other federal, state, or private assistance  

[12:2:66,391] programs.  

[13:0:66,409] 4275 - SOCIAL SERVICES AND LICENSING  

[14:0:66,427] The Department of Social Services oversees and monitors the administration of social services programs, which include child  

[14:1:66,437] welfare, adoptions, licensing and special programs. The department is responsible for development of policy, regulations, and  

[14:2:66,447] procedures that govern the delivery of services to children, families and other recipients, and the monitoring and evaluation of  

[14:3:66,457] the service delivery system.  

[15:0:66,475] 4275010 - In-Home Supportive Services:  

[16:0:66,493] The In-Home Supportive Services (IHSS) program provides in-home services that enable eligible individuals to remain safely in  

[16:1:66,503] their own homes as an alternative to out-of-home care. Eligible persons are low-income aged, blind, or disabled individuals who  

[16:2:66,513] either qualify for federally funded Medi-Cal or meet the program's income and resource requirements. There are four programs  

[16:3:66,523] that provide in-home care: the Personal Care Services Program, IHSS Plus Option Program, Community First Choice Option,  

[16:4:66,533] and IHSS-Residual Program.  

[17:0:66,551] 4275019 - Children and Adult Services and Licensing:  

[18:0:66,569] The Children's Services component consists of three major areas: Child Welfare Services, Adoptions, and Child Abuse  

[18:1:66,579] Prevention.  

[19:0:66,597] Child Welfare Services provides emergency response, family maintenance, family reunification, and permanent placement and  

[19:1:66,607] prevention services to protect abused, neglected or exploited children. The services are provided through an integrated  

[19:2:66,617] services delivery system that provides intensive services to families to promote child safety, permanency and well-being with  

[19:3:66,627] the goal of allowing families to stay together in their own homes, or arrangement for the child's placement in the safest and  

[19:4:66,637] least restrictive home-like setting. Services also include assistance to youth who are emancipating or have emancipated from  

[19:5:66,648] foster care. The program also provides training and technical assistance to county administrators and staff.  

[20:0:66,665] In Child Welfare Services, the Department of Social Services is implementing continuum of care reforms codified in Chapter  

[20:1:66,676] 773, Statutes of 2015. The reforms emphasize home-based family care, improve access to services without having to change  

[20:2:66,686] out-of-home placements to get those services, and increase the role of children, youth, and families in assessment and case  

[20:3:66,696] planning.  

[21:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[2:0:166,32] 5180   Department of Social Services - Continued 

[3:0:66,69] The Adoptions Program provides support services to children and adoptive families through a collaboration of public and  

[3:1:66,79] private adoption agencies in the state. Agency adoptions provide adoption services through public and private agencies for  

[3:2:66,89] children who have been abused, neglected or exploited and are under the jurisdiction of the county or tribal court. Services  

[3:3:66,99] include adoptive placement screening; home studies; reimbursement of non-recurring adoption expenses for adoptive parents;  

[3:4:66,109] training, recruitment and retention of foster parents; and technical assistance and support for inter-country adoptions. For  

[3:5:66,120] independent adoptions, the public agency investigates a proposed adoption and provides a report to the court when the  

[3:6:66,130] biological parents place their children directly with adoptive parents of their choice.  

[3:7:66,148] The Child Abuse Prevention Program provides funding, training, and technical assistance for the development and  

[3:8:66,158] sustainability of child abuse prevention and early intervention programs, education and outreach materials, activities, and  

[3:9:66,168] services for at risk families and their children.  

[4:0:66,186] The Adult Protective Services program provides funding for counties to address reports of physical and financial abuse and  

[4:1:66,196] neglect or exploitation of elder or dependent adults and provide intervention, as necessary.  

[4:2:66,214] The Community Care Licensing Program is a regulatory enforcement program with the responsibility of protecting the health  

[4:3:66,224] and safety of children and adults residing in or spending a portion of their time in out-of-home care. The program includes  

[4:4:66,234] facility licensure, prevention, compliance, and enforcement components.  

[4:5:66,252] 4275028 - Special Programs:  

[5:0:66,269] The Special Programs provides funds for Foster Care Burial, Assistance Dog Special Allowance, Access Assistance to the  

[5:1:66,280] Deaf, Refugee Programs, Immigration and Naturalization Assistance Services and Legal Services for Unaccompanied and  

[5:2:66,290] Undocumented Minors.  

[5:3:66,307] 4280 - TITLE IV-E WAIVER  

[6:0:66,325] The Title IV-E California Child Well-Being Project is a federal waiver demonstration project in California. This project provides  

[6:1:66,335] participating counties with a capped federal grant that in turn provides flexibility in the use of federal and state foster care  

[6:2:66,346] maintenance and administrative funds on program and services expenditures that were previously unallowable.  

[6:3:66,363] 4285 - DISABILITY EVALUATION AND OTHER SERVICES  

[7:0:66,381] The objective of this program is to determine an applicant's medical and/or vocational eligibility for disability benefits and  

[7:1:66,391] provide administrative services to other agencies.  

[7:2:66,409] 4285010 - Disability Evaluation:  

[8:0:66,427] The Disability Evaluation Program determines the medical, vocational, and/or functional eligibility of California residents  

[8:1:66,437] applying for benefits under Title II (Disability Insurance), Title XVI (Supplemental Security Income), and Title XIX (Medicaid) of  

[8:2:66,447] the Social Security Act. Eligibility is determined by the severity of the individual's physical and/or mental impairment(s) and  

[8:3:66,457] overall ability to engage in substantial gainful employment.  

[8:4:66,475] 4285019 - Services to Other Agencies:  

[9:0:66,493] In addition to providing support services for its programs, the Department of Social Services provides general administrative  

[9:1:66,503] services, such as personnel and accounting to the State Council on Developmental Disabilities and the Health and Human  

[9:2:66,513] Services Agency. The Department provides services to the Medi-Cal Program in the form of state hearings and public  

[9:3:66,523] information services.  

[9:4:66,541] 9900 - ADMINISTRATION  

[10:0:66,559] The objective of the Administration program is to provide overall management, planning, policy development, and  

[10:1:66,569] administrative support services to other departmental programs.

[3:0:66,76] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[4:0:66,94] 4350 - STATE-LOCAL REALIGNMENT  

[5:0:66,115] The objectives of Realignment are to assign program responsibility to the most appropriate level of government and achieve  

[5:1:66,125] improved service levels with broad discretion given to the responsible entity. Realignment provides for greater funding stability  

[5:2:66,135] for selected programs, increased local flexibility in administering these programs, and productive fiscal incentives to encourage  

[5:3:66,145] cost-effective approaches to providing services.  

[6:0:66,166] Total Realignment revenues are comprised of a half cent sales tax and a dedicated portion of vehicle license fee revenues.  

[6:1:66,176] Revenues are deposited into the Local Revenue Fund, which includes several accounts. Funds deposited in these accounts  

[6:2:66,186] are continuously appropriated for allocation to local governments according to formula and are used to fund programs specified  

[6:3:66,196] in realignment legislation. The legislation also includes local maintenance of effort and matching requirements in order to  

[6:4:66,207] ensure that counties do not use the realigned funds to supplant local expenditure levels prior to realignment. This provision  

[6:5:66,217] ensures compliance with other state and federal statutes which, in turn, provide hundreds of millions of dollars annually for  

[6:6:66,227] county health and social services programs.  

[7:0:66,268] DETAILED EXPENDITURES BY PROGRAM

[0:0:66,13] HEALTH AND HUMAN SERVICES   2019-20 STATE BUDGET — HHS   221 

[1:0:202,43] 5196   2011 State-Local Realignment  

[1:1:66,64] Building upon the 1991-92 Realignment, 2011 Realignment moves program and fiscal responsibility to counties, providing a  

[1:2:66,74] dedicated source of funding while eliminating duplication of effort, generating savings, and increasing flexibility.  

[1:3:66,95] Realigned programs include local public safety programs, mental health, substance abuse, foster care, child welfare services,  

[1:4:66,105] and adult protective services. Many of these programs are already administered at the local level by counties. Therefore, it is  

[1:5:66,115] appropriate for the programmatic and fiscal responsibility to reside with the counties with the state maintaining an oversight and  

[1:6:66,125] technical assistance role where needed. These changes are made with the goal of providing services more efficiently and at  

[1:7:66,135] less cost.  

[1:8:66,156] The funding sources for realignment are:  

[1:9:65,174] • The dedication of 1.0625 cents of a state special fund sales tax.  

[1:10:65,190] • The dedication of a portion of vehicle license fee revenues.  

[2:0:66,218] Counties receive 2011 Realignment funding from the following accounts and their related growth accounts:  

[2:1:65,235] • Protective Services Subaccount (Foster Care, Child Welfare Services, and Adult Protective Services)  

[2:2:65,252] • Behavioral Health Subaccount (Early and Periodic Screening, Diagnosis, and Treatment; Mental Health Managed Care;  

[2:3:76,262] Substance Abuse Treatment; and Women and Children's Residential Treatment)  

[2:4:65,278] • Mental Health Account (Community Mental Health Programs)  

[2:5:65,294] • Trial Court Security Subaccount  

[3:0:65,310] • Enhancing Law Enforcement Activities Subaccount (Local Jurisdiction for Lower-level Offenders and Parole Violators and  

[3:1:76,321] Adult Parole)  

[3:2:65,337] • Community Corrections Subaccount  

[3:3:65,353] • District Attorney and Public Defender Subaccount  

[4:0:65,369] • Juvenile Justice Subaccount (consisting of the Youthful Offender Block Grant Special Account and Juvenile Reentry Grant  

[4:1:76,379] Special Account)  

[5:0:66,407] The funding reflected below and in the associated special display titled "2011 Realignment Estimate" is an estimate based on  

[5:1:66,417] statutory formulas and the most recent Department of Finance revenue figures.  

[6:0:66,438] Note the $5 billion in   2018-19 and $5.2 billion in 2019-20 shown below reflect the Health and Human Services public safety  

[6:1:66,448] programs. This display does not reflect the funding for the non-Health and Human Services public safety programs. For the full  

[6:2:66,458] list of funding in 2011 Realignment, refer to the special display titled "2011 Realignment Estimate."
